  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_fd226379-65f9-4689-8384-fad44fa5c49b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer9389447330025351327">Ages ago, sorcerers of unmatched power sundered a world into four realms--sky, stone, fire, and water--then vanished. Over time, magicians learned to work spells only in their own realms and forgot the others.   <span id="freeText9389447330025351327" style="display:none">Ages ago, sorcerers of unmatched power sundered a world into four realms--sky, stone, fire, and water--then vanished. Over time, magicians learned to work spells only in their own realms and forgot the others. Now only the few who have survived the Labyrinth and crossed the Death Gate know of the presence of all four realms--and even they have yet to unravel the mysteries of their severed world...<br /><br />In Arianus, Realm of Sky, humans, elves, and dwarves battle for control of precious water--traversing a world of airborne islands on currents of elven magic and the backs of mammoth dragons. But soon great magical forces will begin to rend the fabric of this delicate land. An assassin will be hired to kill a royal prince--by the king himself. A dwarf will challenge the beliefs of his people--and lead them in rebellion. And a sinister wizard will enact his plan to rule Arianus--a plan that may be felt far beyond the Realm of Sky and into the Death Gate itself.</span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fantasy lovers</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6586338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13460620681054077488">Book one in a 7 book series. I LOVE the series. Let me say this, if you think 'oh no it's just another fantasy series', think again. Yeah it sure seems that way, till you get further in... and you start realizing some of the plot, and the timeline... just WHEN it happens will interest you! Some books drag, some are better, but the last 2 books are my favorite.<br/><br/>Book 1 however is action packed and hooks you in quickly.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1753407273" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1753407273" />
    <a title="Tom Quinn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31467977-tom-quinn"><img alt="Tom Quinn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574458226p2/31467977.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1753407273?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom Quinn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom Quinn" href="/user/show/31467977-tom-quinn">Tom Quinn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1753407273" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14939907812929222399">Imagine something like the grand mythos of Tolkien adapted for the stage by an exuberant community theatre company. Sure, there are faults but their edges are softened by enthusiasm and you can easily lose yourself in the grandiose, scene chewing theatrics. There's action, excitement, comedy, magic, political intrigue... Fans of swords and sorcery in any form will find something to love in this wide-ranging series. <br/><br/>4 stars out of 5. Bigger than the sum of its parts, and loads of fun.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_126075381" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/126075381" />
    <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar"><img alt="Dirk Grobbelaar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545117991p2/3102740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/126075381?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dirk Grobbelaar" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar">Dirk Grobbelaar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer126075381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5621605677765797093">This is certainly an example of 'thinking out of the box' as far as world building is concerned. I'm not too sure how to approach a review of this book. I've never read the Death Gate Cycle before, and I must say that this book left me intrigued. I did, initially, have a struggle wrapping my mind around the world of Arianus and the different realms. The maps and diagrams in the front of the book certainly helped. One or two of the characters left me cold, but that didn't really alter my reading </span>
  <span id="freeText5621605677765797093" style="display:none">This is certainly an example of 'thinking out of the box' as far as world building is concerned. I'm not too sure how to approach a review of this book. I've never read the Death Gate Cycle before, and I must say that this book left me intrigued. I did, initially, have a struggle wrapping my mind around the world of Arianus and the different realms. The maps and diagrams in the front of the book certainly helped. One or two of the characters left me cold, but that didn't really alter my reading experience. Let's face it, the world(s) being presented here is almost a character in its own right. I did enjoy the surprises and twists, although the intrigue (political and otherwise) being presented here is not nearly on the same level as what can be found in other series'. I think that actually helps the plot in this case, where too much skulduggery could seriously bog things down. There are secrets and conspiracies though, and enough adventure to keep the pages turning. I would recommend this to people who intend reading the whole series. It's blatantly obvious that some loose ends are only going to be resolved right at the very end. Like I mentioned, I wasn't sure how to approach this review. I couldn't help but feel it might have been better to wait until I've finished book seven. On the other hand, by then I would likely have forgotten what I wanted to say in the first place.<br /><br />Anyway, I'll not go into plot details. This series has a large following, it seems, and most folk likely already know what it's about. It is Fantasy, with just the slightest touch of Mechanical Sci-Fi (if that is even a term). I enjoyed it and will check out the sequels. Oh, and the cover art is pretty cool too. So, if you're into Dragonlance era Fantasy that is reminiscent of Dragonlance whilst still being something else entirely, you might want to check this out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5621605677765797093" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1307818575?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/43848120-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1307818575" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15140688295827402829">I split the review for this up... Too long = too lazy to read (admit it). I first read these as a teenager and I was completely and utterly hooked. It’s been roughly fifteen years since then, and of course, the reading experience changed.<br/><br/>This is sci-fi-fantasy at its hugest form. Tolkien has created a massive fantasy world, in all its glory. The Death Gate Cycle can rival Middle-earth in its magnitude, though I’m not sold on its ability to speak to people’s imagination. Weis and Hickman wrote so</span>
  <span id="freeText15140688295827402829" style="display:none">I split the review for this up... Too long = too lazy to read (admit it). I first read these as a teenager and I was completely and utterly hooked. It’s been roughly fifteen years since then, and of course, the reading experience changed.<br /><br />This is sci-fi-fantasy at its hugest form. Tolkien has created a massive fantasy world, in all its glory. The Death Gate Cycle can rival Middle-earth in its magnitude, though I’m not sold on its ability to speak to people’s imagination. Weis and Hickman wrote something that entwines sci-fi and fantasy, and adds tons of physics, magic and very nonsensical moments to the mix. <br /><br />This book is character-driven and it is hard not to get involved. From the unreadable Patryn, Haplo, to the lamentable Jonathan (book 3 Fire Sea), to the overconfident, proud Xar, and the very intriguing and one-of-a-kind (truly!) Zifnab; I always felt like W &amp; H had done their utmost to create characters you wanted to read more about.<br /><br />When you’ve grown used to Alfred, you can actually feel other characters' despair, most notably Haplo, when Alfred – once again – faints, in the face of danger. As their bond grows, I was often torn between “God no!” and “Hell yes!”: I love how in the end they interact like life-long friends. Dare I use the word "bromance"? Hell, yes.<br /><br />It is impossible not to feel endearment and frustration at the interaction and evolution of the relationship between Jarre and Limbeck, the dwarven rebel couple in book 1, Dragon Wing.<br /><br />One can only love the dog, who roughly goes by that name “dog!”, and who is ridiculously important for Haplo. Won’t say. Spoilers. He has personality and is written with endearing expression and emotion.<br /><br />Bane, the extremely manipulative tyke of a child. I was happy to see how his fate turned, sorry-not-sorry. For someone so small, he caused a lot of trouble and truly got on my nerves.<br /><br />I'll get to Hugh the Hand and Haplo elsewhere. These characters were the reason I got sucked into the stories. What, how, why, when? Take me on this adventure and show me all this world has to offer!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15140688295827402829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_316067012" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/316067012" />
    <a title="H. P." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5389927-h-p"><img alt="H. P." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310482917p2/5389927.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/316067012?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="H. P." class="user" itemprop="url" name="H. P." href="/user/show/5389927-h-p">H. P.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5389927-h-p?shelf=modern-sf">modern-sf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer316067012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16999744885032538603">Dragon Wing is book 1 of 7 in The Death Gate Cycle. The Death Gate Cycle is set in the far future, a post-apocalyptic world that looks a lot like traditional fantasy worlds—full of humans, elves, and dwarves. The difference are two races, Patryns and Sartans (demigods in their own minds). Their war led to the Sundering of the world. The Patryns were imprisoned in the hellish Labyrinth and the world was split into four—one for each of the old elements. The Death Gate Cycle follows a Patryn escape</span>
  <span id="freeText16999744885032538603" style="display:none">Dragon Wing is book 1 of 7 in The Death Gate Cycle. The Death Gate Cycle is set in the far future, a post-apocalyptic world that looks a lot like traditional fantasy worlds—full of humans, elves, and dwarves. The difference are two races, Patryns and Sartans (demigods in their own minds). Their war led to the Sundering of the world. The Patryns were imprisoned in the hellish Labyrinth and the world was split into four—one for each of the old elements. The Death Gate Cycle follows a Patryn escapee from the Labyrinth, Haplo, as he explores the four worlds on behalf of his lord. It’s those four disparate worlds that make the Death Gate Cycle special. Weis and Hickman tread heavily on the well trodden ground of fantastic racism. But the four worlds allow them to examine it from four different perspectives in rapid succession as the first four books focus on a different world. The Death Gate Cycle is epic fantasy but the nature of the worlds allows the introduction of tropes from post-apocalyptic and science fiction, injecting much-needed originality into the genre. It makes for one of the more underrated epic fantasy series in my opinion.<br /><br />Dragon Wing takes place on Arianus, the world of Air. Arianus is composed of “islands” of porous rock floating on bubbles of lighter-than-air gas. The elves travel by mechanical-magic airships and the humans travel by dragon. The dwarves are trapped on the lowest level of the world operating the Kicksey-winsey as virtual slaves of the elves. Haplo steps into the world of an assassin, a crown price, an evil wizard, a reluctant revolutionary, and a bumbling chamberlain. As good as the Death Cycle gets, a great small story is interwoven with Haplo’s larger story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16999744885032538603" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2154921628" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2154921628" />
    <a title="Jim C" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10296231-jim-c"><img alt="Jim C" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340034171p2/10296231.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2154921628?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim C" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim C" href="/user/show/10296231-jim-c">Jim C</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6425186-dragon-wing">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2154921628" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17350650471481841642">This is the first book of a fantasy series from the authors who were responsible for the origins of Dragonlance. In this one, we are introduced to a land that has different realms. These realms could either be higher or lower than each other and they have their own story. Each realm is known but at the same time remains a mystery to the other realm's residents.<br/><br/>I would classify this as epic fantasy as there was so much going on but it never got bogged down in the details. There were aspects of su</span>
  <span id="freeText17350650471481841642" style="display:none">This is the first book of a fantasy series from the authors who were responsible for the origins of Dragonlance. In this one, we are introduced to a land that has different realms. These realms could either be higher or lower than each other and they have their own story. Each realm is known but at the same time remains a mystery to the other realm's residents.<br /><br />I would classify this as epic fantasy as there was so much going on but it never got bogged down in the details. There were aspects of subjugation of races, revolution, and idolatry. Immediately I was intrigued by this book as we were introduced into the character of Hugh the Hand. He is an assassin who is hired to kill a child. I was invested in the characters and the mystery of why a child was to be killed. I knew there was more than meets the eye and there was. There are several races of sentient beings in this book and I liked the conflict in between these races. This is an interesting world and is vast in its scope. With some fantasy novels trying this huge undertaking, the description can get stuck in a mire with its details. That never happens in this book as the pace is terrific throughout.<br /><br />I was impressed by the huge undertaking of conceiving this world. With a little bit of humor thrown in the reader is intrigued by the characters and the mystery of where this book is heading towards. This is the first book so it left a lot on the table but I look forward to exploring these stories.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17350650471481841642" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_364855166" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/364855166" />
    <a title="Charty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/607703-charty"><img alt="Charty" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194487603p2/607703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/364855166?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charty" href="/user/show/607703-charty">Charty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer364855166" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7583767984121911714">I'm re-reading the Death Gate Cycle because it's been a long time and it seemed like a good summer series. The first book is amazingly spry in that they don't bog it down with endless details and make it carry the entire world-building burden. Plus they are pretty sneaky by starting the reader off with a main character (Hugh the Hand) who isn't really the main character at all, yet he makes a good entry point for the reader. You think you are getting some pretty standard fantasy/medieval realm s</span>
  <span id="freeText7583767984121911714" style="display:none">I'm re-reading the Death Gate Cycle because it's been a long time and it seemed like a good summer series. The first book is amazingly spry in that they don't bog it down with endless details and make it carry the entire world-building burden. Plus they are pretty sneaky by starting the reader off with a main character (Hugh the Hand) who isn't really the main character at all, yet he makes a good entry point for the reader. You think you are getting some pretty standard fantasy/medieval realm story and then you realize that this will be something quite different. Enough details about the world and upcoming conflict are hinted at, but the world and story can be enjoyed as a stand alone effort in this volume. Especially engaging are the Gegs and their world involved in Kicksey-Wicksy, a giant machine that no one quite remembers what it's supposed to do, and yet the entire race of Dwarves lives to serve it (and actually worship it). Our main antagonists, Haplo and Alfred are introduced and by the end of the book I was sucked back in and ready to read the next one. A good start and I thought this held up surprisingly well after so many years away.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7583767984121911714" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1419048257" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1419048257" />
    <a title="Silvera Starling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48020974-silvera-starling"><img alt="Silvera Starling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446352265p2/48020974.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1419048257?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Silvera Starling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Silvera Starling" href="/user/show/48020974-silvera-starling">Silvera Starling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1419048257" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18223911158735139331">A good book, but with some noticeable flaws.<br/><br/>The world building is really great and unique, definitely the highlight of the book for me. Instead of seeing the usual fantasy world and culture that is in most novels, this one is very out-of-the-box thinking when it comes to that aspect. It seems everywhere you go, it's the usual: the elves are the magical hippies, the dwarves are the earth/mountain people, and the humans are everything else. Plus dragons. Dragon Wing is pretty good at avoiding all </span>
  <span id="freeText18223911158735139331" style="display:none">A good book, but with some noticeable flaws.<br /><br />The world building is really great and unique, definitely the highlight of the book for me. Instead of seeing the usual fantasy world and culture that is in most novels, this one is very out-of-the-box thinking when it comes to that aspect. It seems everywhere you go, it's the usual: the elves are the magical hippies, the dwarves are the earth/mountain people, and the humans are everything else. Plus dragons. Dragon Wing is pretty good at avoiding all those cliches.<br /><br />However, the characters are dull and forgettable. Writing this review, I can only think of three of them off the top of my head that really stand out. Characterization is weak in this novel. All the focus goes on into the setting with little to the development and changes in the characters. Some characters we get the focus on for a bit and some interesting changes (I won't spoil it), but for the most part, anything huge that happens to any of the people in the story is just shrugged off because there's no connection between the reader and the character, so there's no reason to care.<br /><br />If you're really into fantasy worlds, definitely check this book out. If you're more into fantasy characters, you might want to skip this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18223911158735139331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91736123" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer6134754947367166880">I decided to re-read my favorite fantasy series of all time, The Death Gate Cycle. I was recently telling a friend and her husband (and you know who you are, Emily) how wonderful these books were, and as I was talking to them, I managed to talk myself into re-reading the books.<br/><br/>Hundreds of years ago, the Sartans (a magical race) Sundered the world, dividing it into four components (air, stone, fire, and water) in order to prevent their enemies, the Patryns, from gaining control of the earth. The </span>
  <span id="freeText6134754947367166880" style="display:none">I decided to re-read my favorite fantasy series of all time, The Death Gate Cycle. I was recently telling a friend and her husband (and you know who you are, Emily) how wonderful these books were, and as I was talking to them, I managed to talk myself into re-reading the books.<br /><br />Hundreds of years ago, the Sartans (a magical race) Sundered the world, dividing it into four components (air, stone, fire, and water) in order to prevent their enemies, the Patryns, from gaining control of the earth. The Sartan cast the Patryns into the Labyrinth, a nightmarish prison with danger around every corner. And having done all these things, the Sartans disappeared, leaving the survivors to deal with their new worlds on their own. <br /><br />Reading this book again was like meeting old friends after twenty years and finding that they hadn't changed at all. I almost cried when Alfred made his first appearance (I missed Alfred)...and Hugh the Hand, and Haplo, and Limbeck. The characters are wonderful, and this series is unique among fantasy series.</span>

I’m glad to catch up on the series as I’ve been meaning to read it for quite some time. The world-building is decent. The Sky Realm where this book is set has been split apart by a powerful race of magicians long ago. As such, the highest realm is too cold to sustain life without sever magic intervention. The middle realm which is the most resource-rich lacks access to water, and the lower realm is tr</span>
  <span id="freeText10053861499169816861" style="display:none">This is the first book of the Death Gate Cycle that I never got around to reading in the 1990s. I’m glad to catch up on the series as I’ve been meaning to read it for quite some time. The world-building is decent. The Sky Realm where this book is set has been split apart by a powerful race of magicians long ago. As such, the highest realm is too cold to sustain life without sever magic intervention. The middle realm which is the most resource-rich lacks access to water, and the lower realm is trapped below and drowned by an overabundance of water and storm. As political factions from each realm crash into each other as a consequence of their individual searches for power and better lives, the world’s long-held status quos are unheaved. This story didn’t blow me away, but I wasn’t expecting it to. It is a stereotypical fantasy tale with humans, dwarves, elves competing for power and of course dragons and magic. <br /></span>

The character development of this book is unrealistically advanced, to the point that you have several main characters. They complement and contrast other characters in this book.   <u>Margaret Weis</u>

The character development of this book is unrealistically advanced, to the point that you have several main characters. They complement and contrast other characters in this book. The storyline takes you from reality and puts you into a time line which is unknown to you, and that to progress forward into the book is to learn of the past. The trek through a foreign and awe-inspiring world combined with the different personalities and development of characters pushes this tale forward, as if itself were on a journey.</span>

<div id="review_3435142206" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3435142206" />
    <a title="Leonardo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1747855-leonardo"><img alt="Leonardo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455290276p2/1747855.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3435142206?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leonardo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leonardo" href="/user/show/1747855-leonardo">Leonardo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553057270" href="/book/show/1617555.Dragon_Wing">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Lovers of D&amp;D and modern sword&amp;sorcery novels</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1747855-leonardo?shelf=fantasy-and-science-fiction">fantasy-and-science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1747855-leonardo?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1747855-leonardo?shelf=role-playing">role-playing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1747855-leonardo?shelf=novels-and-short-stories">novels-and-short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3435142206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5036025507627506048">I originally read Dragon Wing in the early 90s, at the peak of my Dungeon & Dragons phase (before I moved to Call of Cthulhu and Vampire), when my brother and I read as many Dragonlance and Forgotten Realms books that we could get hold of. And, of course, since Weis and Hickman wrote the original Dragonlance novels, we got our fist dive into the Death Gate Cycle... and our last for several years, since the next books were not available where we lived. Now that my brother has finally gotten hold </span>
  <span id="freeText5036025507627506048" style="display:none">I originally read Dragon Wing in the early 90s, at the peak of my Dungeon &amp; Dragons phase (before I moved to Call of Cthulhu and Vampire), when my brother and I read as many Dragonlance and Forgotten Realms books that we could get hold of. And, of course, since Weis and Hickman wrote the original Dragonlance novels, we got our fist dive into the Death Gate Cycle... and our last for several years, since the next books were not available where we lived. Now that my brother has finally gotten hold of the whole series, I decided to finally take a proper dive into the world(s) of the Death Gate. And I must say that, once again, I was transported to a land of magic and adventure that I would love to explore in a years-long role-playing campaign. <br /><br />Sorry for the long introduction, but nostalgia will undoubtedly get in the way of any objectivity I might have when reading this series, particulary this book. Nevertheless, I understand that readers nurtured in the realpolitik brutality of <i>A Song of Fire and Ice</i> and other contemporary sword and sorcery novels will find the political intrigue of the Death Gate cycle a little naïve. Fortunately, Weis and Hickman created enough interesting characters and an enrapturing plot with unexpected plot twists that actually make sense. Of course, the greatest achievement in this first book are the first flashes of a much wider and complex world (worlds, actually) that will be fully fleshed in the following novels. An ancient world divided in the four classic elements by well-meaning almost-all-powerful wizard/demigods, allowed the authors to play with four different possibilities for the clichéd combination of humans, elves, and wizards. From other reviews, it seemed they were quite successful and I hope to reach the same conclusion at some point next year. <br /><br />A niche addition to the story is a little essay on the way magic works in this world which is actually quite interesting and thoughtful. Once again, as readers, we get the feelings that the authors were fully engaged in the creation of this world and its background, and that they were not just spitting out funny sounding names and having generic adventurers fight endless hordes of generic monsters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5036025507627506048" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Stifynsemons" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7180172-stifynsemons"><img alt="Stifynsemons" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stifynsemons" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stifynsemons" href="/user/show/7180172-stifynsemons">Stifynsemons</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer4539651385568048442">Dragon Wing is almost one of the rare 5 star stories. Set in a world that is bizarre and novel in construction, but self consistent, different races live segregated lives. The pacing of how they get tied together is excellent and keeps the interest in the story high. <br/><br/>Several of characters, notably Limbeck and Alfred are memorable, and the Gegs in general reminds me of the Monopods in The Voyage of the Dawn Treader at some level. I think the flaws in the story are not so much the characters thems</span>
  <span id="freeText4539651385568048442" style="display:none">Dragon Wing is almost one of the rare 5 star stories. Set in a world that is bizarre and novel in construction, but self consistent, different races live segregated lives. The pacing of how they get tied together is excellent and keeps the interest in the story high. <br /><br />Several of characters, notably Limbeck and Alfred are memorable, and the Gegs in general reminds me of the Monopods in The Voyage of the Dawn Treader at some level. I think the flaws in the story are not so much the characters themselves but the transitions in personality and perspective seem a little bit forced.<br /><br />I will definitely be reading more books in this series.</span>

<div id="review_109656543" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/109656543" />
    <a title="kingshearte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3031302-kingshearte"><img alt="kingshearte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573912877p2/3031302.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/109656543?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="kingshearte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="kingshearte" href="/user/show/3031302-kingshearte">kingshearte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to kingshearte by: </span>
      Don
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3031302-kingshearte?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3031302-kingshearte?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3031302-kingshearte?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer109656543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer668755624182006181">I say I don't read fantasy, but fantasy titles do keep popping up here occasionally. It's my husband's fault. He reads the stuff, and sometimes he gets on me to read certain titles too. However, this is leading me to the conclusion that my husband has excellent taste in fantasy, because anything he has recommended to me (and he certainly doesn't recommend it all to me - he's never suggested I should read any of the vast array of roleplaying novels out there, for example) has actually been very g</span>
  <span id="freeText668755624182006181" style="display:none">I say I don't read fantasy, but fantasy titles do keep popping up here occasionally. It's my husband's fault. He reads the stuff, and sometimes he gets on me to read certain titles too. However, this is leading me to the conclusion that my husband has excellent taste in fantasy, because anything he has recommended to me (and he certainly doesn't recommend it all to me - he's never suggested I should read any of the vast array of roleplaying novels out there, for example) has actually been very good. First there was the Guy Gavriel Kay, then Neil Gaiman (kind of a double endorsement there, from both him and the ex-roommate), and now the Death Gate Cycle.<br /><br />And I must say, I did not have high expectations for this one. It shares many characteristics with the sort of fantasy that makes me say I don't read fantasy. It's long (7 books at 400 or so pages of rather small print may not be as long as some, but it's not short). It involves not one, but four (kind of five or six, actually) entirely invented worlds. And it's full of your typical humans, elves and dwarves, and the wizards of those races. You have your oppressed and your oppressors, and the fight for freedom. You have your inter-race conflict, yada yada yada.<br /><br />But I was pleasantly surprised. The intrigue started almost immediately, and the writing style didn't make me want to shoot myself. Some twists were telegraphed for miles, but not to the point of beating you over the head with them, for the most part. At one point in the middle, I kind of wanted to get on with something happening, but then it picked up again.<br /><br />And I think that this method of developing a series in new worlds is very effective. A major downfall of many fantasy book 1s is that you have to spend so much time introducing the world and its characters that there isn't always much room left for much in the way of story. By choosing to write the first four books of this series as more or less stand-alones, they were able to avoid that. True, the conflicts that happened in this book are only the precursors to the epic one that will presumably arise and take over the latter three books, but they're still basically meaningful, and it doesn't feel like nothing more than interminable set up. They also do a pretty good job, just generally, of making the world-building flow with the story. You don't have pages upon pages of description of the world and its hierarchy and history, and all that; it's just worked in fairly seamlessly, making it a much more pleasant read.<br /><br />It also doesn't go insane with the characters. Many fantasy epics make you want to devote an entire wall in your house to mapping out the characters so you can keep track. This one, by the end of the book had, I would say, eight major characters, and of them one hasn't yet been named and is not really a major player yet, but I expect he will be, and another is dead. There's a small handful of minor players who may or may not develop larger roles, and there's another handful of named incidentals who seem at this point unlikely to be particularly important going forward. So all in all, there are probably no more than 25 named characters in this book. At no point was I confused as to who was who, and who was related how to whom. Which, in my experience, is fairly unusual for high fantasy.<br /><br />Ultimately, I think it's unlikely to become one of my favourite books ever, but it's certainly an enjoyable read, and I think from now on I shall trust my husband's judgement in such matters without question. </span>
  <a data-text-id="668755624182006181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_273491258" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/273491258" />
    <a title="David Sarkies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5856247-david-sarkies"><img alt="David Sarkies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470027282p2/5856247.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/273491258?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sarkies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sarkies" href="/user/show/5856247-david-sarkies">David Sarkies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5856247-david-sarkies?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer273491258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10233409993263939712"><b>I only ever read book one</b><br/>6 February 2012<br/><br/>	Another fantasy novel that was given to me by a friend who told me that it was good so I should read it, and I did, a long time ago. Back in those days I really did not have huge amounts of money, so would generally borrow books from the library or off friends. The problem with borrowing books from the library is that you generally have between two to four weeks to read them, which is not really a problem if you can devote your entire time to reading book</span>
  <span id="freeText10233409993263939712" style="display:none"><b>I only ever read book one</b><br />6 February 2012<br /><br />	Another fantasy novel that was given to me by a friend who told me that it was good so I should read it, and I did, a long time ago. Back in those days I really did not have huge amounts of money, so would generally borrow books from the library or off friends. The problem with borrowing books from the library is that you generally have between two to four weeks to read them, which is not really a problem if you can devote your entire time to reading books. If you, like me, end up borrowing more than you can read then you have a problem, though most book libraries that I know do not charge for borrowing books.<br />	Somebody said in their review, 'if you think this is just another fantasy novel, then you are mistaken'. Well, I would probably say that it is just another fantasy novel, set in a strange fantasy world, with maybe an interesting plot, but nothing all that substantial or world altering. To me, this is just a story, and while it may be moving away from the Lord of the Rings clones, looking back at this time makes me think that I would have done better to read real books, but then again back then I really did not know what a real book was, and wouldn't have even tried to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1420.Hamlet" title="Hamlet by William Shakespeare" rel="nofollow noopener">Hamlet</a> if my life depended on it.<br />	This series in set in a fantasy future where the world have been splinted into five realms, Earth, Air, Fire, Water, and the Labyrinth. The splintering of the world was caused by a war between two races, one of which were imprisoned in the Labyrinth. However, the other race vanished, and one of the lurkers in the labyrinth found a way out, and wants to release his people so that they may return to the world.<br />	This story is set in the realm of air, a realm consisting of numerous floating continents. It seems that it is divided between the upper and lower reaches, with the elves living above and the dwarves below. In a way it does seem similar to other fantasy novels, with elves, dwarves, dragons, and strange human cultures. Obviously it is always a struggle to create a unique culture, but to do that one needs to understand culture. However, I think I will leave this book here, as there is little more I wish to write about it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10233409993263939712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Courtney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2582023-courtney"><img alt="Courtney" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/149034334?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Courtney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Courtney" href="/user/show/2582023-courtney">Courtney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer149034334" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7270804623149080915">OK ok ok, any fantasy lover should truly consider reading this book series. It is the perfect example of what real fantasy is, as it should be, rather then this odd fad with writing bad fantasy. In my Mytholoy class we studied fantasy and there are six rules that Tolkein set for the genera and if those rules arent fallowed then it is not fantasy. Now what I am saying is not that there are rules on writing, which there should never be, but when LOTR what written there were six elements that made </span>
  <span id="freeText7270804623149080915" style="display:none">OK ok ok, any fantasy lover should truly consider reading this book series. It is the perfect example of what real fantasy is, as it should be, rather then this odd fad with writing bad fantasy. In my Mytholoy class we studied fantasy and there are six rules that Tolkein set for the genera and if those rules arent fallowed then it is not fantasy. Now what I am saying is not that there are rules on writing, which there should never be, but when LOTR what written there were six elements that made it fantasy and if those elements are not present or explained, ie. new hero archytypes must be explained, then it is a bad fantasy. This also take into consideraton of other generas such as sci fi ect, but if an author wishes it to be fantasy then they had better study LOTR first.<br />The plot structure and charactor development in this book were (as to be expected) briliant and there wasnt any stepping stones skipped over. One of the worst things for me in a book or series is when suddenly the characters develpoment is stopped or that there is something missing. But in this book you can feel the charactors changing as you read and the plot makes sense even with its own mysteries in the book. The questions you are left asking make sense rather then you just sitting at the last page saying to yourself, (or in my case my mom) "What the hell? Why is _____going there?" or "Wait, wait, why did ________ happen?" But you are still intrigued by a real mystery and all the information that you have makes sense. There are no loop holes that you as the ready can identify nor is there any loop holes un explored by the charactor. I hope that this makes sense because it is hard trying to sum up 8 months of literary study in a review to explain what makes to book good or bad.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7270804623149080915" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=gods-and-elements">gods-and-elements</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=epic">epic</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91261898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1462268053446215044">It's been a long time since I have seriously enjoyed a fantasy novel. Strange, since I still consider it my favorite genre. Somehow, this book was what I needed to get back. From start to end, I enjoyed it and wanted to read more about it.<br/><br/>All the characters, for one, are really well-developed. They are all so multi-faceted that its hard to figure out who you want to support (They are all kinda against each other, but team up at times). My favorite character is the assassin, Hugh the Hand and Alf</span>
  <span id="freeText1462268053446215044" style="display:none">It's been a long time since I have seriously enjoyed a fantasy novel. Strange, since I still consider it my favorite genre. Somehow, this book was what I needed to get back. From start to end, I enjoyed it and wanted to read more about it.<br /><br />All the characters, for one, are really well-developed. They are all so multi-faceted that its hard to figure out who you want to support (They are all kinda against each other, but team up at times). My favorite character is the assassin, Hugh the Hand and Alfred, who faints with disturbing regularity. 10 year old Bane scares me, but he has a lot to offer in character. <br /><br />The story is linear (no weird flashbacks) and is told with grace, avoiding flowery language and excessive description, the general turn-off for me from this genre. Thinking back to the plot, nothing much really happened, but while reading it, it was very interesting and paced well. A lot of things came together during the end of the book, but I still have so many unanswered questions. Which means I have the read the next few book. Its an introductory novel, setting up the world of Gegs (dwarfs), Humans, Elves, and Wizards.<br /><br />I recommend this to anyone who has enjoys fantasy novels. Its a nice next step for Harry Potter lovers. </span>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144435061" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18081971907317720269">I am given this first volume a reluctant three stars, but I don't recommend the series.<br/><br/>In the mid 80's Weis and Hickman wrote the first Dragonlance novels which were very popular. I quite liked them as a teen (although after rereading this series, I'm afraid to revisit them). Since Dragonlance they have worked on a number of other series but never as successfully as the first. Perhaps the most ambitious is The Death Gate Cycle, seven books set across five worlds each with its unique ecology and </span>
  <span id="freeText18081971907317720269" style="display:none">I am given this first volume a reluctant three stars, but I don't recommend the series.<br /><br />In the mid 80's Weis and Hickman wrote the first Dragonlance novels which were very popular. I quite liked them as a teen (although after rereading this series, I'm afraid to revisit them). Since Dragonlance they have worked on a number of other series but never as successfully as the first. Perhaps the most ambitious is The Death Gate Cycle, seven books set across five worlds each with its unique ecology and politics. And it fails miserably.<br /><br />I think the root cause of the failure might be too much world building, so much that all the other elements didn't receive enough attention. All of the many characters beyond the main two are invariably shallow. The prose frequently hits speed bumps as the authors force in explanations of their world building that aren't needed by the story. The "humor" is a one note act recycled from Dragonlance that would be booed out of open mic night. And the plot...the plot resolution after seven volumes is that we should choose love and friendship over hatred, delivered with the subtlety of a Saturday Afternoon Special.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18081971907317720269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah-Jayne Briggs" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah-Jayne Briggs" href="/user/show/800513-sarah-jayne-briggs">Sarah-Jayne Briggs</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer662443691" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15081379297431692302">(This review may contain spoilers).<br/><br/>I think it's really difficult to find any truly unique fantasy books, but this was at least an interesting concept, with a mix of fantasy and technology. The characters were quite well-rounded - and I particularly liked Alfred.<br/><br/>I have to say, I felt sorry for Bane for part of the book, but he was a complete brat for most of it. I'm not sure even Haplo could be classed as a true villain - I felt for him as much as Bane, though in a different way. I suppose he com</span>
  <span id="freeText15081379297431692302" style="display:none">(This review may contain spoilers).<br /><br />I think it's really difficult to find any truly unique fantasy books, but this was at least an interesting concept, with a mix of fantasy and technology. The characters were quite well-rounded - and I particularly liked Alfred.<br /><br />I have to say, I felt sorry for Bane for part of the book, but he was a complete brat for most of it. I'm not sure even Haplo could be classed as a true villain - I felt for him as much as Bane, though in a different way. I suppose he comes under the category of 'villain who does do some nice things'.<br /><br />I'm not sure there were any truly good characters, apart from Alfred. He amused me greatly at times, with his clumsiness and habit of fainting every time something bad happened. The whole concept with the song and the elves was interesting - I'd like to know more about how and why the song actually affects them.<br /><br />The Gegs were particularly likable, though I was sorry to see Limbeck and Jarre's relationship end. I look forward to seeing more with these characters - I have the other six books, so I'll be reading the second one soon.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1515779706244858979">A huge wow for this book, I do think this is my very favourite book so far in the dragonlance series and it is the first book from the death gate cycle. loved it because it spoke about a tiered world, with the gegs (dwarves) being the ones on the bottom rung, totally exploited by other beings who proclaimed themselves to be gods and afraid of the elves!! finally as all subjugated peoples do, a small faction started to rebel, and foment unrest amongst the gegs, the factree where they worked to pr</span>
  <span id="freeText1515779706244858979" style="display:none">A huge wow for this book, I do think this is my very favourite book so far in the dragonlance series and it is the first book from the death gate cycle. loved it because it spoke about a tiered world, with the gegs (dwarves) being the ones on the bottom rung, totally exploited by other beings who proclaimed themselves to be gods and afraid of the elves!! finally as all subjugated peoples do, a small faction started to rebel, and foment unrest amongst the gegs, the factree where they worked to provide water for the gods and the machine which kept them enslaved started to cause questions to be asked, then they found a human (god) who turned out not to be a god and excepted this himself and the revolution started for real!! Bane I hate, he is such a double dealing self interested being, enthralling everyone with his beauty and guiless face and young age, he will need to be watched and his powers curtailed!! Am dying to read the next book as I love revolutions!!!</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ld4LqIL34/+A10DmgyZdeHCC6zB5p31zsdoglnKzytPjCjMiL/YJhxbevCs7wgNqYHktl2zzfnBJLKhy5B+DkA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

<span id="freeTextContainer14913873403433648339">Fantasy novelist who, along with Tracy Hickman, was one of the original creators of the <i>Dragonlance</i> game world. I've written numerous novels and short stories set in the world of Krynn, as well as series in other, original worlds. These include: Darksword, Rose of the Prophet, Star of the Guardians, DeathGate, Dragonvarld, Sovereign Stone, Dragonships, and the Dragon Brigade. I also wrote two para</span>
  <span id="freeText14913873403433648339" style="display:none">Fantasy novelist who, along with Tracy Hickman, was one of the original creators of the <i>Dragonlance</i> game world. I've written numerous novels and short stories set in the world of Krynn, as well as series in other, original worlds. These include: Darksword, Rose of the Prophet, Star of the Guardians, DeathGate, Dragonvarld, Sovereign Stone, Dragonships, and the Dragon Brigade. I also wrote two paranormal romance novels, Fallen Angel and Warrior Angel, with my daughter, Elizabeth Baldwin. I graduated from the University of Missouri–Columbia and now live in Wisconsin with dogs, Max, Dixie, Joey the Thug and Clancy the Hooligan. <br /><br />I am currently working on the third book in the Dragon Brigade series, the Seventh Sigil. The first book is Shadow Raiders. The second book is Storm Riders, coming out from Tor in July 2013. <br /><br />My hobby is flyball racing with my dogs, Dixie, a border collie, and two crackhead Shelties, Joey the Thug and Clancy the Hooligan. <br /><br />I am the owner of the company, Margaret Weis Productions, publisher of RPGs. Our newest project is creating the RPG for the wonderful TV series, Firefly. Shiny!</span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1611445-dragon-wing-the-death-gate-cycle-1">Quotes from Dragon Wing</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Truth wasn't something you went out and found. It was wide and vast and deep and unending, and all you could hope to see was a tiny part of it. And to see that part and to mistake it for the whole was to make of Truth a lie.&rdquo;</span>
